It was a sleeper hit, initially overshadowed by  Barbie  and  Oppenheimer  when it was first released last month. Now, it&amp;apos;s one of the highest-grossing movies released in the US this year.  Jim Caviezel (who played Jesus in Mel Gibson&amp;apos;s movie The Passion of the Christ), stars as Tim Ballard, the real-life Homeland Security Agent who creates a charity to combat child traffickers.  But for many reasons, separate from the heavy subject matter at the focus of the film, the movie is leaving people uncomfortable.  And now it&amp;apos;s available across cinemas in Australia - with Dendy cinemas (co-owned by Mel Gibson) also screening the movie, citing &amp;#x201C;overwhelming demand&amp;#x201D;. In a tweet promoting the movie, the film&amp;apos;s distributors said, &amp;quot;Break the Silence. Save The Children,&amp;quot; a popular phrase coined by QAnon.  The movie was shot in 2018, at a time  when the American conspiracy theory movement, QAnon,  was starting to gain traction.  And its script was written in 2015, well before the movement&amp;apos;s emergence in 2017, its writer and director Alejandro Monteverde told entertainment news publication Variety. While the film, made by Angel Studios, tells a non-partisan story and doesn&amp;apos;t reference QAnon, believers of the conspiracy theory have latched onto the film, promoting it for their own agenda.  QAnon followers believe that left-leaning elites in government, Hollywood stars and billionaires run a paedophile and human trafficking ring. They also believe that these people are harvesting an adrenaline-like substance from children to attain eternal life. Former US President Donald Trump is also thought by followers to be waging a secret battle against this &amp;#x201C;deep state&amp;#x201D; scheme.  It hasn&amp;apos;t helped that lead actor Caviezel has repeated several QAnon phrases on conservative talk shows like &amp;quot;andrenochroming,&amp;quot; the false term used to describe the extraction of a substance from child victims to harvest the elixir of youth. He has also used other language of the movement (&amp;quot;a big storm is coming&amp;quot;) and in 2021, attended a QAnon-adjacent conference. Aside from QAnon believers, the movie is being championed by other notable conservative figures like Trump, who hosted a viewing party at his golf course with Caviezel and the agent who inspired his role in attendance.  Monteverde, who did not attend, said the political ties from others were hurting his film, and he prefers to keep his distance.  In Sound of Freedom, Caviezel as Ballard takes on a crime syndicate in Colombia after children are snatched by strangers.  This depiction has stoked concern from human and child trafficking experts who say while people can be kidnapped by strangers and trafficked, it&amp;apos;s not the typical way it&amp;apos;s done. Typically, it&amp;apos;s done by someone who knows the person and exploits that trust. Now, experts are concerned the hype around this film could actually do more harm than good and prevent people from spotting the most common - actually foreseeable - warning signs.  Elizabeth Campbell, co-director of the University of Michigan&amp;apos;s Human Trafficking Clinic, told NPR: &amp;quot;By doing that, I think we make actual victims of human trafficking more invisible and more vulnerable to exploitation.&amp;quot; World&amp;apos;s Children, a charity supporting vulnerable children, says poor families with financial struggles and debt, and kids who have run away or are homeless are most at risk of being trafficked. Explaining this one requires some context.  The Sound of Freedom was independently filmed in 2018, on a budget of about $14.5m ($22.1m), but was delayed when its distributor, 21st Century Fox, was bought by Disney in 2019.  The COVID-19 pandemic exacerbated the delay, and then in 2023, distribution rights were acquired by Angel Studios.  Angel Studios is a self-described values-based company, though others call it faith-based, as it is behind a number of Christian movies and shows. Before distributing original content, Angel Studios made its brand by removing nudity, swearing and violence from mainstream movies and shows before it was sued by a number of well-known Hollywood studios for copyright.  To raise the $5m ($7.8m) the company needed to distribute and market the film, it crowdfunded the money from &amp;quot;angel&amp;quot; investors. One of the film&amp;apos;s many investors, Fabian Marta, was arrested on 23 July and charged as an accessory for child kidnapping in the US state of Missouri, NewsWeek reported. While the details of the case are not public, this charge carries a penalty of 10 to 30 years in prison or life imprisonment. It&amp;apos;s true the film has been unexpectedly popular, grossing more than the latest Mission: Impossible and Indiana Jones movies in the US.  But some of these sales are being called into question.  In the film&amp;apos;s closing credits, the hero of the film, Caviezel, asks viewers to &amp;#x201C; pay it forward &amp;#x201D; by buying someone else a ticket. It&amp;apos;s unclear how many of those tickets actually translated into actual views, but people online have noticed that the theatres have sometimes been more vacant than online seat availability suggests.  On the Angel Studios site, under the heading, &amp;quot;How can I join the fight to end child trafficking?&amp;quot; the creators say, &amp;quot;Seeing the film is the first step in spreading awareness about child trafficking,&amp;quot; before suggesting to pay it forward or claim a free ticket.  Paying it forward will help you &amp;quot;join a historical movement to promote stories that amplify light,&amp;quot; it writes.  In the last paragraph, there is a link giving viewers a different resource (other than paying it forward).  Answering another question asking what will happen to extra funds, if tickets aren&amp;apos;t claimed, Angel Studios said on its website, &amp;quot;Remaining funds from Pay it Forward may also be used to help the filmmaker create additional content.&amp;quot;","publisher":{"@type":"Organization","name":"SBS News","url":"https://phoenix.prod.edsprd01.aws.sbs.com.au/news","logo":{"@type":"ImageObject","url":"https://www.sbs.com.au/_next/static/img/news/schema-logo-d79dd3e.png","width":"144","height":"144"},"sameAs":["https://www.facebook.com/sbsnews/","https://twitter.com/sbsnews/","https://www.instagram.com/sbsnews_au","https://www.tiktok.com/@sbsnews_au","https://www.youtube.com/user/WorldNewsAustralia","https://www.sbs.com.au/news/feeds"]},"author":[{"@type":"Person","name":"Michelle Elias"}],"articleSection":"Australia","url":"https://phoenix.prod.edsprd01.aws.sbs.com.au/news/the-feed/article/qanon-kidnapping-charges-and-overhyped-ticket-sales-the-sound-of-freedom-movie-cant-escape-controversy/t15hym935","datePublished":"2023-08-24T06:02:48.308Z","description":"Protecting children from traffickers is a dignified cause. Australia</h1><h2 class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-subtitle1 css-1l6oeto" data-testid="article-description">Protecting children from traffickers is a dignified cause. But this movie has been caught in a web of controversy.</h2></div></div><div class="css-eck1d1"><div class="MuiBox-root css-14nolla" data-testid="hero-media"><img sx="[object Object]" alt="A young girl looking alarmed on a bed. MuiTypography-body2 css-vcrtg6" data-testid="heroImageCaption">Jim Caviezel (right) as Tim Ballard in Sound of Freedom. The movie has been swamped in controversy.<span itemProp="name" data-testid="leadImageSource"> Credit: <!-- -->Angel Studios</span></p></div></div><div class="MuiBox-root css-1expiat"><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-body1 css-14foryq" id="article-body" data-layer-event-source-global="Sound of Freedom: An anti-trafficking movie endorsed by QAnon has just landed in Australia"><div><span>The action-thriller Sound of Freedom has now been released in Australian cinemas - but its arrival is riddled with baggage. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>It was a sleeper hit, initially overshadowed by </span><div class="MuiBox-root css-68lxg3" data-layer-event-source-placement="body" data-layer-event-source-title="embeded link" data-layer-event-source-type="embeded link"><a data-layer-event-source="{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;click&quot;,&quot;eventName&quot;:&quot;clickSource&quot;}" class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-inherit MuiLink-root MuiLink-underlineAlways css-16ql34u" target="_self" data-testid="internal-link" href="/news/article/is-barbie-a-feminist-icon-or-just-a-money-making-machine/u0ztoer8d"><span>Barbie</span></a></div><span> and </span><div class="MuiBox-root css-68lxg3" data-layer-event-source-placement="body" data-layer-event-source-title="embeded link" data-layer-event-source-type="embeded link"><a data-layer-event-source="{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;click&quot;,&quot;eventName&quot;:&quot;clickSource&quot;}" class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-inherit MuiLink-root MuiLink-underlineAlways css-16ql34u" target="_self" data-testid="internal-link" href="/news/article/why-a-scene-in-oppenheimer-is-causing-outrage-in-this-country/f3ne2tldd"><span>Oppenheimer</span></a></div><span> when it was first released last month. Now, it&apos;s one of the highest-grossing movies released in the US this year. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Jim Caviezel (who played Jesus in Mel Gibson&apos;s movie The Passion of the Christ), stars as Tim Ballard, the real-life Homeland Security Agent who creates a charity to combat child traffickers. </span><br/><br/></div><div class="css-1v0kanf"><div class="MuiGrid-root MuiGrid-container MuiGrid-direction-xs-column css-i2ezv1"></div></div><div><span>But for many reasons, separate from the heavy subject matter at the focus of the film, the movie is leaving people uncomfortable. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>And now it&apos;s available across cinemas in Australia - with Dendy cinemas (co-owned by Mel Gibson) also screening the movie, citing &#x201C;overwhelming demand&#x201D;. In a tweet promoting the movie, the film&apos;s distributors said, &quot;Break the Silence. Save The Children,&quot; a popular phrase coined by QAnon. </span><br/></div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><h3 data-testid="embed-heading">The first controversy: The QAnon support</h3></div><div><span>The movie was shot in 2018, at a time </span><div class="MuiBox-root css-68lxg3" data-layer-event-source-placement="body" data-layer-event-source-title="embeded link" data-layer-event-source-type="embeded link"><a data-layer-event-source="{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;click&quot;,&quot;eventName&quot;:&quot;clickSource&quot;}" class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-inherit MuiLink-root MuiLink-underlineAlways css-16ql34u" target="_self" data-testid="internal-link" href="/news/article/why-qanon-is-attracting-so-many-followers-in-australia-and-how-it-can-be-countered/23l0ujm0g"><span>when the American conspiracy theory movement, QAnon, </span></a></div><span>was starting to gain traction. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>And its script was written in 2015, well before the movement&apos;s emergence in 2017, its writer and director Alejandro Monteverde told entertainment news publication Variety.</span><br/></div><div></div><div><span>While the film, made by Angel Studios, tells a non-partisan story and doesn&apos;t reference QAnon, believers of the conspiracy theory have latched onto the film, promoting it for their own agenda. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>QAnon followers believe that left-leaning elites in government, Hollywood stars and billionaires run a paedophile and human trafficking ring. They also believe that these people are harvesting an adrenaline-like substance from children to attain eternal life. Former US President Donald Trump is also thought by followers to be waging a secret battle against this &#x201C;deep state&#x201D; scheme. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>It hasn&apos;t helped that lead actor Caviezel has repeated several QAnon phrases on conservative talk shows like &quot;andrenochroming,&quot; the false term used to describe the extraction of a substance from child victims to harvest the elixir of youth. He has also used other language of the movement (&quot;a big storm is coming&quot;) and in 2021, attended a QAnon-adjacent conference.</span><br/></div><div class="css-1n43yqx"><div class="MuiBox-root conservative figures like Trump, who hosted a viewing party at his golf course with Caviezel and the agent who inspired his role in attendance. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Monteverde, who did not attend, said the political ties from others were hurting his film, and he prefers to keep his distance. </span><br/></div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><h3 data-testid="embed-heading">The second controversy: Misleading portrayals of child trafficking</h3></div><div><span>In Sound of Freedom, Caviezel as Ballard takes on a crime syndicate in Colombia after children are snatched by strangers. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>This depiction has stoked concern from human and child trafficking experts who say while people can be kidnapped by strangers and trafficked, it&apos;s not the typical way it&apos;s done.</span><br/></div><div class="css-1n43yqx"><div class="MuiBox-root css-yhggzh" itemscope="" itemType="https://schema.org/CreativeWork" width="115" height="65" decoding="async" data-nimg="1" class="css-0" loading="lazy" style="color:transparent;object-fit:cover"/></div><p class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-body1 css-afitid" itemProp="headline">My daughter was taken by a sex trafficker and now has a price tag on her</p></div></a></div></div><div><span>Typically, it&apos;s done by someone who knows the person and exploits that trust. Now, experts are concerned the hype around this film could actually do more harm than good and prevent people from spotting the most common - actually foreseeable - warning signs. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Elizabeth Campbell, co-director of the University of Michigan&apos;s Human Trafficking Clinic, told NPR: &quot;By doing that, I think we make actual victims of human trafficking more invisible and more vulnerable to exploitation.&quot;</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>World&apos;s Children, a charity supporting vulnerable children, says poor families with financial struggles and debt, and kids who have run away or are homeless are most at risk of being trafficked.</span><br/></div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><h3 data-testid="embed-heading">The third controversy: One of the donors was charged with child kidnapping</h3></div><div><span>Explaining this one requires some context. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>The Sound of Freedom was independently filmed in 2018, on a budget of about $14.5m ($22.1m), but was delayed when its distributor, 21st Century Fox, was bought by Disney in 2019. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>The COVID-19 pandemic exacerbated the delay, and then in 2023, distribution rights were acquired by Angel Studios. </span><br/></div><div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><div itemscope="" itemType="https://schema.org/ImageObject" id="10" data-testid="embeded-image"><div class="MuiBox-root css-14nolla"><img sx="[object Object]" alt="A man kneels in front of a child. " sizes="(min-width:1440) 920px, (min-width:960px) 83vw, 100vw" srcSet="https://images.sbs.com.au/21/7a/38ddac6440bfb2a9ab45aacccc12/the-sound-of-freedom-film-still.jpeg?imwidth=320 320w, https://images.sbs.com.au/21/7a/38ddac6440bfb2a9ab45aacccc12/the-sound-of-freedom-film-still.jpeg?imwidth=360 360w, https://images.sbs.com.au/21/7a/38ddac6440bfb2a9ab45aacccc12/the-sound-of-freedom-film-still.jpeg?imwidth=600 600w, https://images.sbs.com.au/21/7a/38ddac6440bfb2a9ab45aacccc12/the-sound-of-freedom-film-still.jpeg?imwidth=960 960w, https://images.sbs.com.au/21/7a/38ddac6440bfb2a9ab45aacccc12/the-sound-of-freedom-film-still.jpeg?imwidth=1280 1280w" src="https://images.sbs.com.au/21/7a/38ddac6440bfb2a9ab45aacccc12/the-sound-of-freedom-film-still.jpeg?imwidth=1280" width="1920" height="1281" decoding="async" data-nimg="1" class="css-0" loading="lazy" style="color:transparent;width:100%;height:100%"/></div><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-subtitle2 css-h2a21c" data-testid="heroImageCaption">Child-trafficking experts are saying the anti-trafficking film could do more harm than good.<span itemProp="name" data-testid="leadImageSource"> Credit: <!-- -->Angel Studios</span></div><meta itemProp="name" content="A man kneels in front of a child. "/><meta itemProp="width" content="1920"/><meta itemProp="height" content="1281"/><meta itemProp="identifier" content="10"/></div></div><span>Angel Studios is a self-described values-based company, though others call it faith-based, as it is behind a number of Christian movies and shows. Before distributing original content, Angel Studios made its brand by removing nudity, swearing and violence from mainstream movies and shows before it was sued by a number of well-known Hollywood studios for copyright. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>To raise the $5m ($7.8m) the company needed to distribute and market the film, it crowdfunded the money from &quot;angel&quot; investors.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>One of the film&apos;s many investors, Fabian Marta, was arrested on 23 July and charged as an accessory for child kidnapping in the US state of Missouri, NewsWeek reported. While the details of the case are not public, this charge carries a penalty of 10 to 30 years in prison or life imprisonment.</span><br/></div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><h3 data-testid="embed-heading">The fourth controversy: The Pay-It-Forward sales are misleading</h3></div><div><span>It&apos;s true the film has been unexpectedly popular, grossing more than the latest Mission: Impossible and Indiana Jones movies in the US. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>But some of these sales are being called into question. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>In the film&apos;s closing credits, the hero of the film, Caviezel, asks viewers to &#x201C;</span><div class="MuiBox-root css-68lxg3" data-layer-event-source-placement="body" data-layer-event-source-title="embeded link" data-layer-event-source-type="embeded link"><a class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-inherit MuiLink-root MuiLink-underlineAlways css-16ql34u" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" data-layer-event-source="{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;click&quot;,&quot;eventName&quot;:&quot;clickSource&quot;}" href="https://www.angel.com/pay-it-forward/sound-of-freedom" data-testid="external-link"><span>pay it forward</span></a></div><span>&#x201D; by buying someone else a ticket. It&apos;s unclear how many of those tickets actually translated into actual views, but people online have noticed that the theatres have sometimes been more vacant than online seat availability suggests. </span><br/></div><div></div><div><span>On the Angel Studios site, under the heading, &quot;How can I join the fight to end child trafficking?&quot; the creators say, &quot;Seeing the film is the first step in spreading awareness about child trafficking,&quot; before suggesting to pay it forward or claim a free ticket. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Paying it forward will help you &quot;join a historical movement to promote stories that amplify light,&quot; it writes. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>In the last paragraph, there is a link giving viewers a different resource (other than paying it forward). </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Answering another question asking what will happen to extra funds, if tickets aren&apos;t claimed, Angel Studios said on its website, &quot;Remaining funds from Pay it Forward may also be used to help the filmmaker create additional content.&quot;</span></div></div><hr class="MuiDivider-root MuiDivider-fullWidth css-1mvwnbo"/><div
